<div id="review_266060266" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/266060266" />
    <a title="Rachel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/298806-rachel"><img alt="Rachel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452743476p2/298806.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/266060266?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel" href="/user/show/298806-rachel">Rachel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/298806-rachel?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer266060266" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13295410779986250457">When vampires and humans went to war there would only be one victor. The vampires. A treaty was enacted to keep the peace. And as long as the voluntary blood donations continued, the humans within the walled cities would remain safe. Protected.<br/><br/>But with the passage of time, many people forgot their promises and refused to give their blood freely. And as the human population began to dwindle, food supplies became limited and many vampires were left starving.<br/><br/>Attacks on the cities increased. Safety </span>
  <span id="freeText13295410779986250457" style="display:none">When vampires and humans went to war there would only be one victor. The vampires. A treaty was enacted to keep the peace. And as long as the voluntary blood donations continued, the humans within the walled cities would remain safe. Protected.<br /><br />But with the passage of time, many people forgot their promises and refused to give their blood freely. And as the human population began to dwindle, food supplies became limited and many vampires were left starving.<br /><br />Attacks on the cities increased. Safety could no longer be guaranteed. And the ruling vampires were more concerned with keeping themselves fed than the safety of their captives or the hunger of the lesser vampires.<br /><br />As delegate, it was Dawn Montgomery’s responsibility to find a middle ground. To keep Lord Valentine happy and to keep the citizens of Denver safe. But as the youngest person to ever accept the role, her lack of experience made others question her ability. And her hatred of vampires hardly made her a neutral party.<br /><br />With tensions escalating, outcry against her growing, an increased demand for blood donations, and vicious attacks on the rise, Dawn wasn’t sure she could keep the peace, let alone survive. And with everyone she loved already taken from her and with nothing left to lose, she wasn’t so sure she cared.<br /><br />Until the day she met Victor. A boy who changed everything. A savior. A hero. A mystery…. A vampire.<br /><br />***<br /><br />Darkness Before Dawn is a dark, gritty and entertaining dystopian vampire story set in a future where vampires rule, keeping humans isolated and locked down in cities for their protection and to keep control. Where the only thing keeping them safe from the hungry vampires outside the city walls is their willingness to donate blood to the ruling vampire lord.<br /><br />And in this world, still ravaged by the war that was waged and lost, the human population is decreasing. And with a limited supply of blood, the starving vampires outside those walls are getting more desperate and keeping them out is becoming more challenging than ever.<br /><br />As more and more vampires breach the city’s defenses, humans have even more reason to fear the night.<br /><br />With a ruthless vampire lord demanding too much from the humans in his territory, a struggle for control within the vampire hierarchy, an even deadlier threat to both vampires and humans emerging, a heroine who is trying to keep the peace treaty intact and an unlikely hero rising amidst the chaos, Darkness Before Dawn offers readers a suspenseful, exciting and at times nail-biting story with a cliffhanger ending that will leave them anxiously awaiting the next installment in the series.<br /><br />In Darkness Before Dawn the authors combined a dystopian world with the paranormal to create a story with an edge that sets itself apart from many of the stories in this genre. The vampires are reminiscent of the cold-hearted, blood-thirsty vampires depicted in horror stories versus love stories, with the exception of a few whose natures appear slightly more humane and one, in particular, who appears almost human.<br /><br />The story has a nice, even pace that picks up at its end along with the action and suspense. But at times there were some issues with the flow. Much of the story moved along easily and flowed naturally, with writing that was engaging, wonderfully descriptive and often beautiful, but there were moments when there was an awkwardness to the writing and where the characters didn’t behave as expected. Even with these bumps, however, the interesting characters and intriguing world are more than enough to keep readers connected to the story.<br /><br />A first book in this new series, Darkness Before Dawn gives readers a little bit of everything. A dark, dystopian future, humanity on the verge of extinction, numerous deadly enemies, unrest among the humans and among the vampires, secrets, lies and betrayals, a love triangle, an ill-fated love story and a cliffhanger ending. Add in action, mystery and tension and this is one story that will captivate fans of the genre.<br /><br />On a personal note:<br /><br />What drew me to this story was the premise. I loved the idea of a world where vampires ruled. Where they weren’t about living in harmony with humans. Where humans were simply their blood supply.<br /><br />I loved the world the authors created. It was dark. It was violent. It was most definitely grim, practically hopeless and extremely isolated. I was easily and immediately transported into the world and I could imagine its crumbling buildings, its fearful citizens, it’s daring and rebellious residents who were just itching for a taste of freedom.<br /><br />And I absolutely adored Victor. He was my favorite character in this book. He was charming. He was brave. He was incredibly fast and strong and smart. And he was a hero. A virtual knight in shining armor at times.<br /><br />While I wasn’t initially a Dawn fan, she did grow on me. And her character did grow over the course of the story, which I always love to see. She was incredibly sympathetic for all she had lost. But for someone who was brave much of the time, she seemed to be a bit of a pushover at others.<br /><br />There were a few twists and turns, one pretty big one, though I wasn’t caught by surprise when it came to light. But it was still an awesome change in direction nonetheless and one that totally made the ending incredibly exciting.<br /><br />I definitely want to know more about the world outside of Denver. I want to know more about the night train. I want to know more about what it means to be a delegate. I want to know more about the lesser vampires and just how things got as bad as they did. I want to know more about the vampires in charge.<br /><br />And I want to know what happens next for Dawn and Victor. As that was one giant cliffhanger the authors left me with.<br /><br />What pulled me out of the story at various times during the read was some of the writing and character development. I thought much of the writing was absolutely beautiful. There were gorgeously written and incredibly meaningful passages. But they often sat side-by-side with some that were more awkwardly written with unusual ways of describing things.<br /><br />At times I felt very connected to the writing and the story and at other times I didn’t. Perhaps it’s because there were two writers involved and their styles didn’t quite blend as smoothly as I might have liked in order to keep me connected. Or perhaps it was simply that I was able to connect to one writer’s style versus another.<br /><br />I was also somewhat surprised by the change in direction with Michael’s character. The picture painted of him was that for years he was the best friend and practically perfect. And all of a sudden he becomes pushy, argumentative, demanding and selfish. With no real explanation given and no lead up to the change.<br /><br />There were a couple instances where Dawn’s actions and reactions felt out of character, too. Even though she’d been through a lot, she was still brave, she still fought for what she thought was right and she took on the responsibility of being a delegate after the deaths of her parents. And yet she allowed herself to be persuaded against her better judgment to attend a party in a dangerous area and go for a wall walk and risk leaving the city because her friends wanted to.<br /><br />But neither were enough to make me want to set this book aside. I did devour it in one sitting. I found myself always wanting to know more. And I couldn’t help but be most curious about Victor and his past.<br /><br />While this wasn’t a brand new idea, the authors did make it their own. I found the world to be intriguing and by the end of the story incredibly exciting. I found characters to love, hate or be exceedingly frustrated with, all of whom I think played an important role and contributed to making this story pretty great.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13295410779986250457" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14237879016715674785" style="display:none">This book seems to tiptoe back and forth across the line of what I consider to be juvenile writing. I like the premise of the storyline though, and I think in the right author’s hands (possibly one that would have written it as adult fiction rather than YA) it could have been amazing. As it is, the writing style is pretty simple, and it’s an easy read. The biggest downfall is the predictability of where the storyline is heading. I suspected that Sin was a vampire right from the introduction of his character. I also suspected that Dawn’s hoodie stalker was actually her brother. The only reason I haven’t rated this as a 1-2 star flop, is the fact that I do like the premise of the storyline. </span>

<div id="review_3554061119" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3554061119" />
    <a title="ShootingStar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/116395548-shootingstar"><img alt="ShootingStar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598580060p2/116395548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3554061119?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ShootingStar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ShootingStar" href="/user/show/116395548-shootingstar">ShootingStar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/116395548-shootingstar?shelf=a-little-confusing">a-little-confusing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/116395548-shootingstar?shelf=annoying-main-character">annoying-main-character</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/116395548-shootingstar?shelf=could-ve-been-better">could-ve-been-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/116395548-shootingstar?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/116395548-shootingstar?shelf=extremely-boring">extremely-boring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/116395548-shootingstar?shelf=got-a-little-annoying">got-a-little-annoying</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/116395548-shootingstar?shelf=infuriating">infuriating</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/116395548-shootingstar?shelf=never-reading-ever-again">never-reading-ever-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/116395548-shootingstar?shelf=non-existent-plot">non-existent-plot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/116395548-shootingstar?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3554061119" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4031902718546980250">So many things about this book were so, so bad. I don't even know where to start. <br/><br/>Here's the thing about paranormal books: they can either go two ways. They could be truly amazing, with an awesome plot, and unique ideas. Or, they could be like the train-wreck that was Twilight, with no plot and absolutely horrific heroines. The latter is more likely. <br/><br/>And this was the same case with this book. <br/><br/>Let me start with the actually story. The whole main idea of this book is incredibly unrealistic. The bo</span>
  <span id="freeText4031902718546980250" style="display:none">So many things about this book were so, so bad. I don't even know where to start. <br /><br />Here's the thing about paranormal books: they can either go two ways. They could be truly amazing, with an awesome plot, and unique ideas. Or, they could be like the train-wreck that was Twilight, with no plot and absolutely horrific heroines. The latter is more likely. <br /><br />And this was the same case with this book. <br /><br />Let me start with the actually story. The whole main idea of this book is incredibly unrealistic. The book follows Dawn, who is supposedly the youngest delegate--someone who goes and discusses with the king vampire. Let me begin by saying that this is highly unlikely. It's like having a governor who is a seventeen-year-old, which will (hopefully) never happen. If the author could not bother to come up with a better backstory other than Dawn's parents died, so she became the new delegate, I have very little hope for the story. <br /><br />On to the characters. If Dawn's best friend is supposed to be portrayed as a supporting and kind person, the author has been sorely mistaken. Tegan (that's her name) is consistently rude to Dawn. In fact, Tegan basically starts the book by calling Dawn a chicken and telling her that she doesn't live her life the way she's supposed to. I very nearly stopped reading. Apparently if you're too scared to go out to a party in the middle of the night because you don't want to get bitten by a damn vampire, you're a chicken. Good to know. <br /><br />The writing in this book was truly horrific. I honestly believe the author has not heard of a compound sentence. There are many, many places in which the author could've made the sentence into one. The writing was incredibly choppy and it annoyed me so, so much. <br /><br />Here's an example: <b> "She knows lots of guys. They all want to know her." </b> <br /><br />Fine the first time? Yes. But if you're forced to keep reading choppy sentences like this? The author could've easily made these two sentences into one: She knows lots of guys, and they all want to know her. <br /><br />See? Easy. But why take the effort to make a compound sentence? <br /><br />On top of that, the writing is incredibly redundant. The author pains to remind us every two sentences about someone's clothing choices. Eventually, it gets so bad that we're treated to a whole page description of Victor's (one of the characters) vampire clothes. Also, the author feels the need to point out that every single person in this book's body is "petite." Dawn's, Tegan's, Lila's, Rachel's...if they're a girl, they're "petite."<br /><br />Diversity, much?<br /><br />Let's get on with the romance. I hated both love interests. Victor, the vampire love interest, comes across as a stalker and a creep. He followed Dawn around everywhere and, when she dares to question him, he assures her it's for her own safety. Michael (who was her current boyfriend when the book started. But then they break up. And get back together again. I'm actually not sure what their relationship is at the end of the book) is overprotective of Dawn in a possessive way. But then, Michael starts acting like a jerk to Dawn in the middle of the book because...well, actually, I'm not entirely sure why. I'm assuming it was to make Victor look like the 'better person' without him actually doing anything significant. So great, then. Michael's a jerk and Victor's still a creep. I actually got so peeved when Victor decides to kiss Dawn, just to tell her that they don't belong together. But clearly, he is suffering from some kind of amnesia, since he forgets all about that two chapters later and kisses Dawn all over again, followed by him telling her that they can't be together. Why give her the false hope? What is wrong with him?<br /><br />On to Dawn herself. She is the most self-pitying, needy, helpless, and annoyingly contradicting main character. She constantly blabbers on about how good she is at fighting, and how self-capable she is. She proves this wrong consistently, however, whenever she gets into situation in which she can show off these 'superior fighting skills.' Instead of beating the crap out the vampires who are pursuing her, she hangs around, waiting for either Victor or Michael to show up and save her sorry butt. If this isn't bad enough, she continuously moans and groans about how terrible her life is since she's a delegate. She spends her days either being terrified of every damn thing, or just sitting around and doing nothing at all. And I swear, if I counted the number of times she started shivering and needed Micheal to show up and comfort her, I would've lost count. <br /><br />And I thought it was really, really stupid when Dawn gets annoyed at Victor for not telling her that he was a vampire on the day the met. I'm sorry, but if I remember correctly, he was too busy saving your life!! And you just met him. What did you expect? For him to spout out his whole life story to you?<br /><br />Oh and I feel the need to say somewhere in here that putting the main character's name in the book title is NOT cool, clever, or cute. <br /><br />I think my biggest problem with this book is that there was no urgency. The author provided no suspenseful moments. The plot was simple and straightforward, going from point A to point B. The few plot twists there were had little impact on the plot and were easy to predict. <br /><br /><br /><b> Quotes that Stood Out To Me </b> <br /><br /><br /><b> "I can almost understand we were so naive." </b><br /><br />What do you mean, almost? And you ARE still naive. Nothing has changed. <br /><br /><br /><b> Most Contradicting Sentence <br /><br />"Neither of us believes in relying on someone else for protection." </b><br /><br />Wow. I would've never guessed. Because from what I can tell, all you ever seem to do is rely on someone else. <br /><br /> <b> Most Stupid Exclamation: <br /><br />"Vampires!" <br /><br />or <br /><br />"He's a damn vampire!" </b><br /><br />These sentences make fun of themselves. <br /><br /><br /><b> Biggest Misunderstanding of the term 'funny' :<br /><br />"Tegan tries to stumble out, but the strap of the seatbelt holds her captive. Victor releases it, and she's scrambling out and staggering farther into the shadows. It would be funny any other night." </b><br /><br />I, for one, found this situation reasonably funny. But Dawn? Tegan's supposed best friend apparently finds it funny to see her best friend drunk and barfing. Wonderful. Glad I don't have Dawn as a friend. <br /><br /><br /><b> Another Contradicting Sentence: <br /><br />Dawn on Rachel's brown eyes: "She has the most boring brown eyes, but she looks better than I ever could." <br /><br />Dawn on Michael's brown eyes: "His eyes are a deep brown, not dull, but rich and dark." </b><br /><br />Okay, so I honestly don't see the big difference here. And since when are brown eyes terribly boring? I personally like brown eyes. <br /><br /><b> Stupidest Sentence: <br /><br />"Any other guy might bring a girl chocolate. But Michael is all about a strong, healthy body." </b><br /><br />Okay, so you can't be strong and healthy AND eat chocolate? Why is this even mentioned? What does this have to do with anything at all?<br /><br /><b> Biggest Misunderstanding of the Term 'arrogance':<br /><br />King Vampire: "You are special, Dawn, in ways you can't fathom."<br /><br />Dawn's reaction: "His arrogance infuriates me." </b><br /><br />Am I missing something here? He just called her special. I mean, he is sorely mistaken, but is that somehow and insult now?<br /><br /><br /><b> Most un-true statement <br /><br />Dawn after having a fight with her enemy Lila: "I take pride in knowing the bigger teacher moved to restrain me, not Lila."</b><br /><br />I honestly thought Lila was winning that fight, so...And if you take some much pride in winning a fight, why don't you bother to fight when your life depends on it?<br /><br /><br /><b> Most unnecessary description: <br /><br />Dawn while getting bitten by a vampire: "I gasp as they penetrate. It hurts." </b><br /><br />Wow. Had no clue, Dawn. I thought it would tickle. Really though, does getting bitten by a vampire actually hurt?<br /><br />Really, beyond ridiculous. <br /><br /><br />Overall, I really disliked this book. The plot was stupid, the main character was horrific, the side characters were arguable worse, and the writing was extremely redundant and repetitive. The writing didn't flow and was extremely choppy. The action's of the characters made no sense, but, considering the whole story, sense apparently isn't what we're going for. Dawn's past was not well explained, and I wanted to know what actually happened to her parents. The only reason I gave this horrid book two stars is because, at some rare parts of the book, a part of me was intrigued. I do not recommend this book, except if you want a good hate read, which is exactly how I'm going to find the strength to plow through the rest of this series. <br /><br />Truly disappointing. If you decide to read this, good luck. You'll need it. <br /><br />Happy Reading!! :) <br /><br />And sorry for such a long review :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="4031902718546980250" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3081722-shelley?shelf=2012-releases">2012-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3081722-shelley?shelf=ya-dystopian">ya-dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3081722-shelley?shelf=publishers-arc">publishers-arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer279094550" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1288884376131234896">*Rating* 4 stars<br/>*Genre* YA Paranormal/Dystopian<br/><br/>J.A. London’s Darkness before Dawn is the first novel in a promising new series that features a world where vampires have won the 30 year war against humans and now live by an agreement called the Vamp-Hu Treaty. In accordance with the treaty, humans are required to provide blood to the vampires and in return, the vampires agreed not to attack any of the remaining US cities. Not all humans are agreeable to the treaty which leads to complications. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText1288884376131234896" style="display:none">*Rating* 4 stars<br />*Genre* YA Paranormal/Dystopian<br /><br />J.A. London’s Darkness before Dawn is the first novel in a promising new series that features a world where vampires have won the 30 year war against humans and now live by an agreement called the Vamp-Hu Treaty. In accordance with the treaty, humans are required to provide blood to the vampires and in return, the vampires agreed not to attack any of the remaining US cities. Not all humans are agreeable to the treaty which leads to complications. The one positive that came out of the Vamp-Hu treaty is that vampires cannot turn humans against their will.<br /><br />The story itself takes place in Denver, Colorado where the city is walled in and armed with hunters called Night Watchmen. The Night Watchmen are responsible for killing any rogue vampires that try to make their way into the city.<br /><br />17 year old Dawn Montgomery is the story’s main protagonist and the official delegate between the humans and vampires. She is required to meet with the most powerful vampire in the world, Lord Valentine, on a regular basis on all matters of concern. Valentine forces her to wear Victorian clothing when meeting with him and he picked her above all others to be the Human representative.<br /> <br />Dawn was chosen for the job after her parents were killed by vampires mysteriously. The reason behind their attack and the secrets that they took to their grave, are hanging like a chad during a presidential election in Florida. There is something about Dawn that is considered special and intriguing but has yet to be revealed.<br /> <br />Michael Colt is Dawn’s best friend, love interest, as well as training to become one of the elite Night Watchmen. He and Dawn do everything together and it's hoped that they would be together forever. Later, Dawn meets vampire Victor Valentine who saves her and her best friend Tegan Romano from a vampire attack. This leads to more complications since Dawn sincerely respects Michael and what he stands for. I normally complain LOUDLY about love triangles but in this case, it was actually done in a way that left me open to Dawn being with either character.<br /><br />Because this is the first book in the series, there are plenty of comparisons to Julie Kagawa’s The Immortal Rules which I actually read AFTER this book. If you want to compare the characters, we can do that.<br />Both Allison and Dawn are strong willed. They are both willing to do whatever it takes in order to survive in a hostile environment where vampires rule the roost. They both lost their parents under circumstances that created a hardship for both characters. One difference is that Dawn actually has a guardian, Rachel Goodwin, to look after her needs. Allison helps herself. They both have series of events that pushes them in a certain direction and their choices are not the best at times.<br /><br />What is best left unsaid is that this book ends with tragedy and a cliffhanger that will hopefully be remedied in the next book called Blood Kissed Sky. The book on one hand is also predictable when it comes to the villain. When this person is introduced, warning bells should have been ringing loudly. Instead, a certain character falls head over heels for him and ends up in an unknown predicament.<br /> <br />I was actually surprised when this book came in the mail. I’m not sure who sent it to me from HarperCollins or who to thank personally. But, I am appreciative and hope that they will continue to share these ARC’s with me in the future.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1288884376131234896" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_277257374" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/277257374" />
    <a title="Rhomy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6897164-rhomy"><img alt="Rhomy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424562609p2/6897164.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/277257374?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rhomy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rhomy" href="/user/show/6897164-rhomy">Rhomy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13347459-darkness-before-dawn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6897164-rhomy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6897164-rhomy?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6897164-rhomy?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6897164-rhomy?shelf=1st-in-a-series">1st-in-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6897164-rhomy?shelf=i-love-that-guy">i-love-that-guy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6897164-rhomy?shelf=have-it-on-paperback">have-it-on-paperback</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer277257374" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11942479415782367090"><b>Schemes, politics, desire for power, envy, jealousy and love, all entangled in a great story.<br/></b><br/><br/>Darkness before Dawn is a great vampire story. Probably one of the best I've read lately.<br/><br/>It is set in the city of Denver in a future where humans are very aware of the existence of vampires. Actually, they've been coexisting since the war thanks to a treaty. This treaty said that vampires would be away of the cities as long as humans donate blood to keep them satisfied. Of course, that didn't last long a</span>
  <span id="freeText11942479415782367090" style="display:none"><b>Schemes, politics, desire for power, envy, jealousy and love, all entangled in a great story.<br></b><br><br>Darkness before Dawn is a great vampire story. Probably one of the best I've read lately.<br><br>It is set in the city of Denver in a future where humans are very aware of the existence of vampires. Actually, they've been coexisting since the war thanks to a treaty. This treaty said that vampires would be away of the cities as long as humans donate blood to keep them satisfied. Of course, that didn't last long and when humans forgot their part, vampires started to forget theirs... and so this story begins.<br><br>Dawn, our protagonist is the youngest delegate in history, she is supposed to keep peace among both species. But things start to get a little messy, especially when a handsome stranger resques her on a dangerous night and attacks start in the city...<br><br>I really enjoyed the premise of this book. It has a complex plot, with non stop action and I couldn't stop turning the pages. <br><br>The writing is great, it just flows. Applause for both authors!!!<br>The world the authors built seems utterly real. I felt transported to that isolated place and I felt the fear of the citizens at night. I wouldn't dare to go out knowing what lurks in the dark. <br><br>Even if I was first drawn to it due to the gorgeous cover and that I'm a total sucker for vampire books, I liked that in Darkness Before Dawn vampires are vampires. I mean, they feed on human blood. Period. You should be scare of them, not fascinated. Except well... for some of them... with intense blue eyes... *sigh* :D<br><br>Yes, it's true, some parts are a little predictable but the road taken to unfold those issues was great IMO.<br><br>Regarding characters, Dawn is strong, she's been training all her life to defend herself and she is brave. Yes, it's a given, sometimes bravery can lead to problems but what kind of book would we have if everything was simple, right?<br>She is also witty and caring, and she allows herself to trust someone even when the world around suggests you shouldn't trust anyone whatsoever. <br><br>Victor, oh my! *sigh* Dark hair, blue eyes, enigmatic and a loner... and with an agenda... yup! he got me after 10 seconds :D<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1389318966i/8019772._SX540_.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br>There is also the almost perfect boyfriend and the best friend Tegan, they were both equally lovable and annoying. <br>I mean, quit getting yourselves in trouble idiots!<br><br>And of course, the evil ones. Which are really evil hehe. Ruthless.<br><br>I believe all the characters are well developed, we get some background of each and they are very easy to relate to.<br><br>The romance is well developed too. It is attraction at first sight but Dawn is smart enough not to get herself caught in the situation.<br>The way the romantic events unfurled was perfectly conceived.<br><br>The end has a major twist and is bittersweet. Left me wanting more.<br><br><b>Definitely I want to read more about these characters and this interesting story.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="11942479415782367090" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_341331224" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/341331224" />
    <a title="Justin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4862284-justin"><img alt="Justin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464472130p2/4862284.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/341331224?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justin" href="/user/show/4862284-justin">Justin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer341331224" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5072849656330832105">As far as YA vampire books go, Darkness Before Dawn was fairly decent. I don't really feel as though it was amazing, but it was an enjoyable read. It mentions several vampire related series in the synopsis, all of which I haven't read yet, so I don't really know if it pulls many elements from them or not. But of the Vampire books I have read, I easily spotted quite a few similarities. I feel like the mother son duo did a good job making the story their own though, even though I didn't really pic</span>
  <span id="freeText5072849656330832105" style="display:none">As far as YA vampire books go, Darkness Before Dawn was fairly decent. I don't really feel as though it was amazing, but it was an enjoyable read. It mentions several vampire related series in the synopsis, all of which I haven't read yet, so I don't really know if it pulls many elements from them or not. But of the Vampire books I have read, I easily spotted quite a few similarities. I feel like the mother son duo did a good job making the story their own though, even though I didn't really pick up on anything that was really new to the genre.<br /><br />As I mentioned above, I really don't feel like there was anything new to the Vampire genre in Darkness Before Dawn. That doesn't mean this is a bad book though, it's really a quite an enjoyable story even if there are outside influence from other works within the genre. The story was pretty basic, war between vampires and humans, romance, family rivalry, etc etc. It's really difficult to talk much about the story, since it's all pretty much things you've heard before. With that said, you really can see the voice of the authors come out in the story, it's hard to jump into a genre like this and try to write something that hasn't been done before. In the end, I really think they did a pretty good job with the story, it just would of been nice to see something new brought to the genre.<br /><br />The characters fall along the same lines as the story in my opinion. They are all enjoyable and well written characters, but they all seem to draw so many parallels to other characters within the YA vampire genre. I am a little more understanding of this, though. I feel like characters are a lot more difficult to build than the plot lines, and having read several big YA vampire books I feel like it's a natural thing to attempt to draw all of these parallels between the characters. I'm not going to go into much detail, the main characters are all pretty decent, I didn't really have a issue with them past what I talked about above.<br /><br />I was pleased with the ending, actually. It was actually one of the most enjoyable parts, in my opinion. There is quite a bit of action towards the end, involving the old family. And a lot of the things that happen with that, have a huge impact on the final outcome of the book. I did feel like the very end was somewhat predictable, based on all of the previous things that happen. But it did make me excited to see what happens in book two, which I feel is the most important thing.<br /><br />In the end, I will say that Darkness Before Dawn is a good book. It's nothing new to the genre, but if you enjoy Vampire books I am sure you will enjoy this one. I did find that it was a much darker vampire book than some that are out there, which always makes books like this much more enjoyable in my opinion. I know I didn't go into to much detail in this review, but like I said there just wasn't much in this book that was really new so I didn't feel as though I needed to go into a massive amount of detail. It's an overall enjoyable book, and the author duo did a very nice job writing it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5072849656330832105" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_241794745" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/241794745" />
    <a title="Brooke" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4140635-brooke"><img alt="Brooke" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476044114p2/4140635.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/241794745?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brooke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brooke" href="/user/show/4140635-brooke">Brooke</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer241794745" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8714246604137460879">I had high hopes for this book. Being a reader who’s over vampires, I needed this book to wow me, dazzle me and not irritate me. Darkness Before Dawn did not disappoint! I was actually surprised at how good it was!<br/><br/>I really liked the writing style in this one. It wove simplistic descriptions with beautiful imagery and I thought the whole book read like a movie. Or at least it did for me! I saw everything play out perfectly in my head. <br/><br/>As for the main character, Dawn, I was actually quite fond of </span>
  <span id="freeText8714246604137460879" style="display:none">I had high hopes for this book. Being a reader who’s over vampires, I needed this book to wow me, dazzle me and not irritate me. Darkness Before Dawn did not disappoint! I was actually surprised at how good it was!<br /><br />I really liked the writing style in this one. It wove simplistic descriptions with beautiful imagery and I thought the whole book read like a movie. Or at least it did for me! I saw everything play out perfectly in my head. <br /><br />As for the main character, Dawn, I was actually quite fond of her! She was smart, determined and not afraid to stand up for herself. Following her parents death, she became the youngest delicate to represent both the vampires and the humans in the city where she lives, so those traits are definitely handy. The only thing I didn’t like about Dawn? The people she hung around with; her boyfriend Michael being one of them. <br /><br />Michael was too perfect for me. Dawn mentioned over and over how perfect they were for each other but I felt nothing between them. They had more of a sibling vibe going on. Also, he was kind of an ass. He wasn’t that supportive of Dawn, and he was more concerned about what a good vamp killer he’d be once he became a Night Watchman. Ugh. I felt that he was too wrapped up in himself. I did not fall for his ‘charms.’<br /><br />I really wasn’t impressed with Dawn’s best friend, Tegan, either. She was bossy and irresponsible; she really only led Dawn into trouble. I didn’t click with her as a character. But, one good thing about Tegan’s recklessness? It led to Victor!<br /><br />Oh my gosh *swoon* I love him. So much. He is sexy and charming and protective and intelligent. Oh yeah, and vampire. And once Dawn found that fact out she never missed a chance to tell Victor how much she despised him; but he was not deterred. He wanted to help her lessen the strain between the vampires and the humans; he insisted that they could work together. <br /><br />So, the more Dawn and Victor spend time together the more she learns about him. Victor does a lot of things to help the citizens of her city and Dawn comes to understand that not all vampires are monsters, especially not Victor. Could she perhaps be falling for this creature of the night? She sure is!<br /><br />Now, Victor and Dawn have CHEMISTRY!! The forbidden-ness of their relationship!? Holy wowza. It was fantastic! But just when things start heating up between them BAM! The end. Oh my Lord Valentine! What the HELL!? How could it end there!? EEEP! That ending was like, whoa. <br /><br />Overall, Darkness Before Dawn was a really good read! If you’re looking for a book that puts a new spin of vampire/human relationships and one that has a dash of delightful romance, then this book is for you! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8714246604137460879" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UM6tcLVur34564/2VoUTz6EpYBZT8dLbSAMwIBd+Vy2YTG0IRwx8n5q5RDsPRaqK1JCny63C94BUaLGL1f4a8A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/+mNbXC8qddUc1iK9UOSpyq8DbIoPwH2EAwe0IooR+g3a00Vgt56Nvchk0esgyviXwXKb9YMJK0MZ597SKgKNQ==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2231072426755937643">J.A. London is the mother-son writing team of Rachel Hawthorne and her son, Alex London. Rachel has written many novels for teens, including the popular Dark Guardian series. Alex, a recent graduate with a degree in Historical Studies, enjoys combining history and fiction to create unique worlds. The Darkness Before Dawn series is their first joint project.</span>
